    ", we will also considerably simplify the descriptions of associators and vertical / horizontal compositions in @xmath33 $ ] , thus providing a useful set of tools for explicit computations in any bicategory of fractions .",

    "if you need to use the constructions described in propositions  [ prop-01 ] , [ prop-02 ] , [ prop-03 ] or  [ prop-04 ] for associators and vertical / horizontal compositions but you do nt remember the precise statements , the general philosophy behind all such results is the following :    a.   firstly , you have to use the set of choices @xmath50 in order to construct the compositions on the level of @xmath4-morphisms of @xmath33 $ ] ( see ) ; b.   now you need to construct a representative of a @xmath3-morphism between the morphisms constructed in ( a ) . if you need to compute associators , jump to point ( c ) below ; if you need to compute compositions of the form ( ii ) and ( iii ) , then the diagram that you want to construct can be partially filled with @xmath3-morphisms of @xmath0 , coming from any chosen representatives for the @xmath3-morphisms that we are composing ; c.   the missing `` holes '' in the diagram that you are constructing can be filled using axioms and finitely many times ( an example of such an iterative procedure can be found in the remarks following each proposition mentioned above ) ;",
    "d.   in general , axioms and do not ensure uniqueness : in ( c ) you might get different `` fillings '' for the holes , and hence different diagrams . the results in propositions  [ prop-01 ] , [ prop-02 ] , [ prop-03 ] and  [ prop-04 ] ensure that different choices in ( b ) and ( c ) induce diagrams representing _ the same @xmath3-morphism _ in @xmath33 $ ] .",
    "so you do not have to worry about the choices made above : you simply take the equivalence class of the diagram that you constructed , and you are done .",

  "abstract_text": [
    "<S> in this paper we investigate the construction of bicategories of fractions originally described by d.  pronk : given any bicategory @xmath0 together with a suitable class of morphisms @xmath1 , one can construct a bicategory @xmath2 $ ] , where all the morphisms of @xmath1 are turned into internal equivalences , and that is universal with respect to this property . </S>",
    "<S> most of the descriptions leading to this construction were long and heavily based on the axiom of choice . in this paper we considerably simplify the description of the equivalence relation on @xmath3-morphisms and the constructions of associators , vertical and horizontal compositions in @xmath2 $ ] , thus proving that the axiom of choice is not needed under certain conditions </S>",
    "<S> . the simplified description of associators and compositions will also play a crucial role in two forthcoming papers about pseudofunctors and equivalences between bicategories of fractions . </S>"
  ]
